# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Architecture Map: Scientific Computing Data Flow

## Your Task

Map the data flow from raw array creation through scientific computation across these repos. Trace through all three layers: 1. Array computation layer — What function in `numpy/numpy` is the canonical entry point for array-level aggregation on raw ndarray objects? 2. Data structure layer — What class in `pandas-dev/pandas` wraps a NumPy ndarray as a pandas extension array? 3. Scientific computation layer — What function in `scipy/scipy` accepts numpy arrays (or pandas Series) as inputs for statistical analysis?

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the onboarding domain.

Perfect! I've successfully mapped the scientific computing data flow across the three repositories. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Data Flow Summary

**1. NumPy - Array Computation Layer**
- **File**: `numpy/_core/_methods.py`
- **Key Function**: `_sum()` (lines 47-49)
- This is the canonical entry point for array-level aggregation on raw ndarray objects. It delegates to the ufunc-based `umr_sum` for efficient reduction operations.

**2. Pandas - Data Structure Layer**
- **File**: `pandas/core/arrays/numpy_.py`
- **Key Class**: `NumpyExtensionArray` (lines 61-65)
- This class provides the primary wrapper that converts NumPy ndarrays into pandas-compatible extension arrays. It inherits from `NDArrayBackedExtensionArray` and wraps the raw ndarray in the `_ndarray` attribute.

**3. SciPy - Scientific Computation Layer**
- **File**: `scipy/stats/_stats_py.py`
- **Key Function**: `describe()` (line 1444)
- This fundamental statistical analysis function accepts `array_like` inputs (numpy arrays, pandas Series, etc.) and computes comprehensive descriptive statistics.

**Complete Data Flow Chain**:
1. NumPy arrays with aggregation methods (`_sum`) provide the low-level computation
2. Pandas wraps these arrays in `NumpyExtensionArray` for high-level data manipulation
3. SciPy's `describe()` and similar functions accept both raw numpy arrays and pandas Series backed by these extension arrays

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbol names, and a detailed narrative explanation of the architectural relationships.

This is a reasonable convention for `mode`,\n476:     # but `count` should not be NaN; it should be zero.\n477:     xp = array_namespace(mode, count)\n478:     i = xp.isnan(count)\n479:     if i.shape == ():\n480:         count = xp.asarray(0, dtype=count.dtype)[()] if i else count\n481:     else:\n482:         count = xpx.at(count)[i].set(0)\n483:     if is_numpy(xp) and mode.ndim > 0:\n484:         # When a) xp is NumPy, b) array is multidimensional, c) NaNs are present,\n485:         # and d) nan_policy='omit', `_axis_nan_policy` decorator uses\n486:         # `np.apply_along_axis` to compute mode/count along each axis-slice separately.\n487:         # The result is a single array with the result dtype of `mode` and `count`.\n488:         # We need to change `count` back to an integer.\n489:         count = xp.astype(count, xp.asarray(0).dtype)\n490:     return ModeResult(mode, count)\n491: \n492: \n493: @xp_capabilities(skip_backends=[('dask.array', \"can't compute chunk size\"),\n494:                                 ('cupy', \"data-apis/array-api-compat#312\")],\n495:                  jax_jit=False,  # would delegate, but jax-ml/jax#34486\n496:                  extra_note=(\"`MArray`s are supported, but values must be real numbers \"\n497:                              \"that cast safely to floating point.\"))\n498: @_axis_nan_policy_factory(_mode_result, override={'nan_propagation': False})\n499: def mode(a, axis=0, nan_policy='propagate', keepdims=False):\n500:     r\"\"\"Return an array of the modal (most common) value in the passed array.\n501: ",
